  <raw>GM expects Brazil to become its third-largest consumer



   General Motors announced  Wednesday that it expects Brazil to become its third-largest  consumer market in 2007, said Ray Young, president of the GM  Brazil subsidiary.

    Sales to the Brazilian market are expected to rise by 10  percent this year, up to 450,000 vehicles. Brazil will then be  able to surpass Canada, which currently occupies third place,  after the United States and China, Young said.
    The company does not plan to increase its market share in  Brazil, where it holds the third-largest share, after Fiat and  Volkswagen. The rise in sales would then follow the general growth of the country's estimated automobile market for 2007, he added.
    The executive also stressed that the main aim is to consolidate the subsidiary within the General Motors Corporation.
    "Operations in Brazil were important to the company's results  in 2006. About 410,000 vehicles were sold on the domestic market,  and the subsidiary's revenues reached 6 billion U.S. dollars last  year, a rise of 12 percent comparing to 2005," Young said.
    In the first months of 2007, demand proved that it was the  beginning of a promising year. GM plants were not able to meet all orders of certain models, which led to customer waiting lists, a  situation Young described as "a good problem."
    "However, since the economies are interconnected, the growth  expected for 2007 could be compromised in the event that market  turbulence, like the current U.S. mortgage market, occurs," he  added.</raw>
